## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (ODE rate laws for concentration vs time)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard object modeled by kinetic rate laws (mass-action, decay, autocatalysis, reversible reactions) as ordinary differential equations in time t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion in excess-reagent or surface-limited regimes)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like decay, many decomposition reactions)
- n-th order (power-law) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global rate law when order is non-integer or unknown)
- Autocatalytic growth/depletion: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (self-amplification with quadratic termination or dimerization)
- General polynomial (mass-action truncation): dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3 (lumped kinetics from multiple parallel steps)
- Reversible first-order relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to steady state A→c1 with timescale 1/c0)
- Reversible with forward/backward contributions: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (net rate from two opposing first-order channels)
- Rational inhibition/activation (effective rate constant depends on A): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A) (self-inhibition / limited active sites without using Hill form)
- Rational with baseline source/sink: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A / (c2 + A) (production minus saturable removal in reactor/biochemical clearance-like kinetics)
- Exponential time-dependent forcing (e.g., catalyst deactivation or temperature ramp effect absorbed into time): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (time-varying first-order rate coefficient)
- Pulsed/periodic forcing (e.g., periodic illumination): dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + sin(c2 * t)) * A (time-periodic modulation of effective rate)
- Biexponential decay mixture (lumped two-pathway time-dependence): dA_dt = -A * (c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t)) (two time-varying channels acting on A)
- Autocatalysis with carrying-like limitation (bounded growth in A): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-catalyzed formation with depletion/limitation by finite capacity c1)
- Singular/strong inhibition near depletion (regularized): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (rate slows strongly at high A; avoids division by zero)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass-action unimolecular steps often appear as linear-in-A terms in dA_dt; multiple parallel first-order pathways sum as dA_dt = -(k1 + k2 + ...) * A.
- Reversible or relaxation-to-equilibrium behavior is typically captured by a linear restoring form dA_dt ∝ (A_eq - A), producing exponential approach to a steady state.
- Autocatalytic or chain-branching mechanisms tend to introduce positive feedback (terms like +A or +A^2) paired with higher-order negative terms (e.g., -A^2, -A^3) that stabilize or terminate growth.
- When apparent rate slows at high concentration due to inhibition, limited sites, or transport limits, rational forms such as A/(c + A) or A/(c + A^2) are common effective laws.
- Time-dependent operating conditions (temperature ramps, catalyst deactivation, switching illumination) often enter as a time-varying prefactor multiplying A or A^n, e.g., k(t)*A with k(t) using exp(c*t), sin(c*t), or low-order polynomials in t.
- If dA_dt remains nonzero as A→0, include a source term (+c) representing feed/production; if dA_dt must vanish at A=0, enforce factors of A in every depletion term.
- Competing mechanisms can yield non-integer effective orders; allowing A**c (c real) can capture composite pathways without explicitly modeling intermediates.
- Stiff kinetics (fast initial drop then slow tail) is often represented by sums of terms with different nonlinearities or time-dependent prefactors, indicating multiple timescales.

1. `A²` term

**Key observation:** The GT contains `sin(log(A+1))`, which is a very specific basis function. No combination of polynomials, exponentials, rational functions, or simple logarithms can reproduce `sin(log(A+1))`. Only candidates containing `sin(log(...))` or equivalent could match.

Let me go through each candidate systematically:

**Candidates with `sin(A*c + c)` terms:** 6, 12, 13, 14, 17, 20, 21, 35, 37, 40
- These have `sin(linear function of A)`, not `sin(log(A+1))`. Since `sin(aA+b) ≠ sin(log(A+1))` for all A, these cannot match.

**Candidates with `log(A*c + 1)` terms:** 15, 16, 18, 22, 25, 26, 27, 36, 38, 41, 42, 43, 44, 45, 46, 47, 48, 49
- These have `log(A*c+1)` which is not `sin(log(A+1))`. A logarithm is linearly independent from `sin(log(...))`.

**Candidates with `exp(A*c)` terms:** 1, 2, 3, 4, 7, 8, 9, 10, 11, 19, 23, 24, 28, 29, 30, 33, 34, 39, 50, 51, 52
- `exp(A*c)` cannot reproduce `sin(log(A+1))`.

**Candidates with power terms `A**c`:** 2, 3, 10, 11, 16, 23, 31, 46
- `A^c` cannot reproduce `sin(log(A+1))`.

**Candidates with `t` polynomial/power terms:** 28, 34, 38, 44
- Extra `t` dependence that doesn't match GT structure, and still missing `sin(log(...))`.

None of the candidates contain the basis function `sin(log(A + c))`. The GT requires this specific nonlinear composition. Since:
- `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be expressed as any polynomial in A
- `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be expressed as `exp(cA)`
- `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be expressed as `log(cA+1)`
- `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be expressed as `sin(cA+d)`
- `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be expressed as any rational function of A
- `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be expressed as `A^c`

None of these candidates can match the GT.
